10076-8{_}906{_}Well, it was plain Duveen could help him and Lister was ambitious, but he frowned and pulled himself up.
10076-8{_}907{_}He was not going to intrigue for promotion and use a girl's friendship in order to force his chiefs to see his merits.
10076-8{_}908{_}Things like that were done, but not by him; it demanded qualities he did not think were his.
10076-8{_}909{_}Moreover he did not know if Ruth Duveen was his friend.
10076-8{_}910{_}She was attractive, but he imagined she was clever.
10076-8{_}911{_}All the same, if he could get the doctor to fix his bandage so as to make it inconspicuous he would dine with the Duveens.
10076-8{_}912{_}CHAPTER VI  WINNIPEG BEACH  Lister went to the opera with his hosts and was moved by the music and the feeling that he was one of a careless, pleasure-seeking crowd.
10076-8{_}913{_}For the most part, his life had been strenuous and the crowds he knew were rude.
10076-8{_}914{_}His home was a bare shack, sometimes built on the wind-swept alkali plains, and sometimes in the tangled woods.
10076-8{_}915{_}From daybreak until dusk fell, hoarse shouts, the clank of rails, the beat of heavy hammers filled his ears, and often the uproar did not stop at dark.
10076-8{_}916{_}When a soft muskeg swallowed the new track, he must watch, by the flaring blast-lamps, noisy ploughs throw showers of gravel from the ballast cars.
10076-8{_}917{_}Labor and concentration had left their mark.
10076-8{_}918{_}Lister's muscles were hard, but his body and face were thin.
10076-8{_}919{_}He looked fine-drawn and alert; his talk was direct and quick.
10076-8{_}920{_}As a rule, his skin was brown, but now the brown was gone, and the lines on his face were deeper.
10076-8{_}921{_}His injury accounted for something and he felt the reaction from a strain he had hardly noted while it must be borne.
10076-8{_}922{_}Although he had not altogether hidden his bandage and his clothes were not the latest fashion, Ruth Duveen was satisfied.
10076-8{_}923{_}Somehow he looked a finer type than the business men in the neighboring stalls.
10076-8{_}924{_}One felt the man's clean virility and got a hint of force.
10076-8{_}925{_}Lister was highly strung.
10076-8{_}926{_}The music stirred his imagination, and when the curtain went down the light and glitter, the perfume that drifted about, the women's dress, and the society of his attractive companion gave him a curious thrill.
10076-8{_}927{_}He began to see he had missed much; ambitions that had forced him to struggle for scope to use fresh efforts took another turn.
10076-8{_}928{_}Life was not all labor.
10076-8{_}929{_}Ruth Duveen had enlightened him.
10076-8{_}930{_}He studied her.
10076-8{_}931{_}She had grace and charm; it was much to enjoy, for one evening, the society of a girl like this.
10076-8{_}932{_}Duveen went off between the acts to meet his friends, but Ruth stopped and talked.
10076-8{_}933{_}Her smile was gracious and Lister let himself go.
10076-8{_}934{_}He told her about adventures on the track and asked about her life in the cities.
10076-8{_}935{_}Perhaps it was strange, but she did not look bored, and when the curtain went down for the last time he felt a pang.
10076-8{_}936{_}The evening was gone and in a day or two he must resume his labor in the wilds.
10076-8{_}937{_}Lister did not cheat himself; he knew the strange, romantic excitement he had indulged would not be his again.
10076-8{_}938{_}When they went down the passage Ruth gave him a smiling glance and saw his mouth was firm.
10076-8{_}939{_}"You look rather tired," she said.
10076-8{_}940{_}"Have we tired you?"
10076-8{_}941{_}Lister turned and his eyes were thoughtful.
10076-8{_}942{_}She had stopped to fasten her cloak, and the people pushing by forced her to his side.
10076-8{_}943{_}An electric lamp burned overhead and her beauty moved him.
10076-8{_}944{_}He noted the heavy coils of her dark hair, her delicate color, and the grace of her form.
10076-8{_}945{_}"I'm not at all tired," he said.
10076-8{_}946{_}"I feel remarkably braced and keen, as if I'd waked up from sleep.
10076-8{_}947{_}In fact, I think I have awakened."
10076-8{_}948{_}Ruth laughed.
10076-8{_}949{_}She saw he was not smiling and his graveness gave her a sense of power.
10076-8{_}950{_}He had owned, with typical frankness, that she had moved him.
10076-8{_}951{_}"Sometimes to wake up suddenly gives one a jolt," she said.
10076-8{_}952{_}"However, you will soon get calm again in the woods."
10076-8{_}953{_}He sensed something provocative and challenging in her voice, but he would not play up.
10076-8{_}954{_}"I wonder--" he said quietly.
10076-8{_}955{_}"In a way, the proper line's to go to sleep again."
10076-8{_}956{_}"Sometimes one dreams!
10076-8{_}957{_}I expect you dream about locomotives breaking through trestles and dump-cars plunging into muskegs?"
10076-8{_}958{_}He laughed.
10076-8{_}959{_}"They're things I know, and safe to dream about.
10076-8{_}960{_}All the same, I rather expect I'll be haunted by lights and music, pretty dresses and faces--"  He stopped, and Ruth remarked: "If these have charm, there are no very obvious grounds for your going without.
10076-8{_}961{_}You can command a locomotive and Winnipeg's not very far from your camp.
10076-8{_}962{_}But we're stopping the people, and I can't fix this clasp."
10076-8{_}963{_}She moved, and the opera cloak fell back from her arm, which was uncovered but for the filmy sleeve that reached a little below the shoulder.
10076-8{_}964{_}He noted its fine curves and the silky smoothness of her skin.
10076-8{_}965{_}Although he fastened the clasp with a workman's firm touch, he thrilled.
10076-8{_}966{_}Then the crowd forced them on and they found Duveen waiting by the car.
10076-8{_}967{_}When they stopped at Lister's hotel Ruth said, "We are going to Winnipeg Beach, Saturday.
10076-8{_}968{_}Would you like to come?"
10076-8{_}969{_}Duveen nodded.
10076-8{_}970{_}"A happy thought!
10076-8{_}971{_}I've got to talk to some business people who make Ruth tired.
10076-8{_}972{_}If you come along, I needn't bother about her."
10076-8{_}973{_}"That's how one's father argues!"
10076-8{_}974{_}Ruth exclaimed.
10076-8{_}975{_}Lister hesitated.
10076-8{_}976{_}"I was told to lie off because I was hurt.
10076-8{_}977{_}If I'm fit to enjoy an excursion, I'm fit to work."
10076-8{_}978{_}"You're too scrupulous, young man.
10076-8{_}979{_}Have a good time when it's possible, or you'll be sorry afterwards.
10076-8{_}980{_}I reckon you're justified to take all the company will give."
10076-8{_}981{_}"It was caution, not scruples.
10076-8{_}982{_}Suppose I meet one of the railroad chiefs?"
10076-8{_}983{_}"I'll fix him," Duveen rejoined.
10076-8{_}984{_}"Your bosses won't get after you when you belong to my party.
10076-8{_}985{_}Anyhow, we'll look out for you."
10076-8{_}986{_}The car rolled off, and Lister, going to the rotunda, lighted a cigarette and mused.
10076-8{_}987{_}Ruth Duveen had beauty, he liked her but must use caution, since he imagined the friendship she had given him was something of an indulged girl's caprice.
10076-8{_}988{_}Then he began to think about the girl he had met on board the train.
10076-8{_}989{_}Now he was able, undisturbed, to draw her picture, he saw she, too, had charm, but she was not at all like Ruth.
10076-8{_}990{_}The strange thing was, one did not note if she were beautiful or not.
10076-8{_}991{_}In a way, this did not matter; her pluck and firmness fixed one's interest.
10076-8{_}992{_}Lister threw away his cigarette.
10076-8{_}993{_}He was poor and not romantic.
10076-8{_}994{_}The girl he had helped had vanished, and after their excursion he hardly expected to see Ruth again.
10076-8{_}995{_}Ruth was kind, but she would soon forget him when he was gone.
10076-8{_}996{_}He would go to Winnipeg Beach with her, and then return to the woods and let his job absorb him.
10076-8{_}997{_}In the meantime, his head had begun to ache and he went to bed.
10076-8{_}998{_}The Saturday morning was typical of Winnipeg in summer.
10076-8{_}999{_}The fresh northwest breeze that sweeps the Manitoba plains had dropped.
10076-8{_}1000{_}Dark thunder-clouds rolled about the sky, but the sun was hot and an enervating humidity brooded over the town.
10076-8{_}1001{_}The perspiring crowd in Main Street moved slackly, the saloon bars were full, and the groups of holiday-makers flocking to the station wore a languid look.
10076-8{_}1002{_}Lister met his hosts in the marble waiting hall where a gold-framed panorama of Canadian scenery closes the view between the rows of stately pillars.
10076-8{_}1003{_}Duveen had brought three or four keen-eyed, nervous business men, a rather imposing lady, and Ruth, and they got on board a local train soon after Lister arrived.
10076-8{_}1004{_}Winnipeg Beach was then beginning to attract holiday-makers from the prairie town.
10076-8{_}1005{_}One could row and fish in sheltered bays, and adventure on board a gasoline launch into the northern wilds.
10076-8{_}1006{_}Boating, however, had no charm for Duveen's friends.
10076-8{_}1007{_}The excursion was an opportunity for friendly business talk, and when lunch was over Ruth and Lister went out on the lawn in front of the hotel.
10076-8{_}1008{_}There was no wind.
10076-8{_}1009{_}A few dark clouds floated motionless overhead, but outside their shadow the lake shone like glass, running back until it melted into faint reflections on the horizon.
10076-8{_}1010{_}A varnished launch flashed in the sun and trailed a long white wake across the water.
10076-8{_}1011{_}"Do you want to stay and talk to Mrs.
10076-8{_}1012{_}Knapp?"
10076-8{_}1013{_}Ruth asked.
10076-8{_}1014{_}"I do not," said Lister.
10076-8{_}1015{_}"Anyhow, I imagine Mrs. Knapp doesn't want to talk to me.
10076-8{_}1016{_}I'm not a big-business man."
10076-8{_}1017{_}Ruth laughed.
10076-8{_}1018{_}"Oh, well, when you speculate at the Board of Trade, a railroad engineer is not a useful friend.
10076-8{_}1019{_}I suppose I ought to stay, but the things one ought to do are tiresome.
10076-8{_}1020{_}Let's go on the lake."
10076-8{_}1021{_}Lister got a canoe, and fixing a cushion for Ruth, picked up the paddle.
10076-8{_}1022{_}"Where shall we go?"
10076-8{_}1023{_}"North, as far as you can.
10076-8{_}1024{_}Let's get away from the boats and trippers and imagine we're back in the woods where you helped me catch the big gray trout."
10076-8{_}1025{_}"Then you liked it at the construction camp?"
10076-8{_}1026{_}Lister remarked.
10076-8{_}1027{_}"It was a pretty rude spot."
10076-8{_}1028{_}"For an indulged city girl?"
10076-8{_}1029{_}Ruth said, smiling.
10076-8{_}1030{_}"Well, perhaps I'd got all the satisfaction dinner parties and dances and the society at hotels can give.
10076-8{_}1031{_}I knew the men who handle finance and work the wires behind the scenes, but I wanted to know the others who do the strenuous things and keep the country going.
10076-8{_}1032{_}I came, and you helped me to understand the romance of the lakes and woods."
10076-8{_}1033{_}Lister did not remember if he had tried to do so and thought he had not.
10076-8{_}1034{_}All the same, the girl was keen and interested.
10076-8{_}1035{_}In summer, it was not hard to feel the lonely sheets of water and tangled bush were touched by romance.
10076-8{_}1036{_}Then, perhaps, everybody felt at times a vague longing for the rude and primitive.
10076-8{_}1037{_}But he was not a philosopher, and dipping the paddle, he drove the canoe across the tranquil lake.
10076-8{_}1038{_}In the meantime, he imagined Ruth studied him with quiet amusement, and wondered whether she thought he was not playing up.
10076-8{_}1039{_}He did not mean to play up; the game was intricate, and, if he were rash, might cost him much.
10076-8{_}1040{_}He had taken off his hat and jacket and effort had brought back the color to his skin.
10076-8{_}1041{_}His thin face had the clean bronze tint of an Indian's; the soft shirt showed the fine-drawn lines of his athletic figure; but Lister was not conscious of this.
10076-8{_}1042{_}He knew his drawbacks, but not all his advantages.
10076-8{_}1043{_}When he had gone some distance and the hotel and houses began to melt into the background, he stopped and let the canoe drift.
10076-8{_}1044{_}"How far shall we go?"
10076-8{_}1045{_}he asked.
10076-8{_}1046{_}Ruth indicated a rocky point, cut off by the glimmering reflection, that seemed to float above the horizon.
10076-8{_}1047{_}"Let's see what is on the other side.
10076-8{_}1048{_}Now and then one wants to know.
10076-8{_}1049{_}Exploration's intriguing.
10076-8{_}1050{_}Don't you think so?"
10076-8{_}1051{_}"Sometimes; in a practical sense.
10076-8{_}1052{_}When a height of land cuts the landscape, I wonder whether one could find an easy down-grade for the track across the summit.
10076-8{_}1053{_}That's about as far as my imagination goes."
10076-8{_}1054{_}"Oh, well," said Ruth, "exploration like that is useful and one doesn't run much risk.
10076-8{_}1055{_}But risk and adventure appeal to some people."
10076-8{_}1056{_}Lister resumed paddling.
10076-8{_}1057{_}The girl had charm and he was young; if he were not cautious, there might be some risk for him.
10076-8{_}1058{_}He was not a clever philanderer, and Ruth and Duveen had been kind.
10076-8{_}1059{_}By and by a puff of cool wind touched his hot skin and he looked round.
10076-8{_}1060{_}A black cloud had rolled up and there were lines on the water.
10076-8{_}1061{_}"We may get a blow and some thunder," he remarked.
10076-8{_}1062{_}"Shall we go back?"
10076-8{_}1063{_}"Not yet.
10076-8{_}1064{_}We'll make the point first.
10076-8{_}1065{_}If it does thunder, summer storms don't last."
10076-8{_}1066{_}He paddled harder and a small white wave lapped the canoe's bows.
10076-8{_}1067{_}The sky was getting dark, and now the lines that streaked the lake were white, but the wind was astern and they were going fast.
10076-8{_}1068{_}The glimmering reflections had vanished and the rocks ahead rose sharply from the leaden water.
10076-8{_}1069{_}The point was some distance off, but Lister knew he must reach it soon.
10076-8{_}1070{_}A flash of forked lightning leaped from the sky and touched the lake, there was a long, rumbling peal, and then a humming noise began astern.
10076-8{_}1071{_}Angry white ripples splashed about the canoe and lumps of hail beat Lister's head.
10076-8{_}1072{_}Then, while the thunder rolled across the sky, the canoe swerved.
10076-8{_}1073{_}It was blowing hard, the high bow and stern caught the wind, the strength was needed to hold her straight with the single paddle.
10076-8{_}1074{_}If he brought her round, he could not paddle to windward, and to steer across the sea that would soon get up might be dangerous.
10076-8{_}1075{_}They must make the point and land.
10076-8{_}1076{_}He threw Ruth his jacket, for spray had begun to fly and the drops from the paddle blew on board.
10076-8{_}1077{_}"Put on the thing; I've got to work," he said.
10076-8{_}1078{_}In a few minutes his work was hard.
10076-8{_}1079{_}Short, white waves rolled past, the canoe lurched and swerved, and Lister knew if she swung off across wind and sea she might capsize.
10076-8{_}1080{_}He must keep her running and let the combers split against her pointed stern.
10076-8{_}1081{_}The combers were getting large and their hissing tops surged by some height above the gunwale, but so long as he could keep her before them they would not come on board.
10076-8{_}1082{_}When her bows went up she sheered, as if she meant to shoot across the hollow left by the sea that rolled by.
10076-8{_}1083{_}He stopped her with a back-stroke and then drove hard ahead, for he must have speed to steer when the next sea came on.
10076-8{_}1084{_}In the meantime, the lightning flickered about the lake and between the flashes all was nearly dark.
10076-8{_}1085{_}The tops of the waves tossed against leaden cloud and he could hardly see the rocks for which he steered.
10076-8{_}1086{_}By and by, however, the point stood out close ahead.
10076-8{_}1087{_}The trees on the summit bent in the wind; spray leaped about the bowlders where the white foam rolled.
10076-8{_}1088{_}He must go round and find a landing to lee, but to go round he must cross the belt of breaking water, with the savage wind abeam.
10076-8{_}1089{_}The canoe shipped some water, and riding in on a comber's crest, narrowly missed a rock that lifted its top for a moment out of the foam.
10076-8{_}1090{_}Then Lister drove her in behind the point and helped Ruth to land on a gravel beach.
10076-8{_}1091{_}Her eyes sparkled and he saw she had not been daunted.
10076-8{_}1092{_}"We're all right now, but we have got to stay until the storm blows out," he said.
10076-8{_}1093{_}They found shelter in a hollow of the cliff and sat among the driftwood while the rain that blotted out the lake drove overhead.
10076-8{_}1094{_}The deluge did not reach them and the cold was going.
10076-8{_}1095{_}"You go back on Monday?"
10076-8{_}1096{_}Ruth said at length.
10076-8{_}1097{_}Lister smiled with humorous resignation.
10076-8{_}1098{_}"I must.
10076-8{_}1099{_}The strange thing is, when I left my job before I was keen to get back.
10076-8{_}1100{_}Now I'd rather stop and loaf."
10076-8{_}1101{_}"Then you were not bored at Winnipeg?"
10076-8{_}1102{_}"Not at all," Lister declared.
10076-8{_}1103{_}"If it would give me a holiday like this, I'd get hurt again."
10076-8{_}1104{_}"I expect the woods get dreary.
10076-8{_}1105{_}Then, perhaps, one doesn't make much progress by sticking to the track?
10076-8{_}1106{_}Don't you want to get into the office where the big plans are made?"
10076-8{_}1107{_}"I don't know," said Lister thoughtfully.
10076-8{_}1108{_}"On the track you're all right if you know your job; at headquarters you need qualities I don't know are mine.
10076-8{_}1109{_}Anyhow, I'm not likely to get there, if I want or not."
10076-8{_}1110{_}Ruth gave him a curious glance.
10076-8{_}1111{_}"Sometimes one's friends can help.
10076-8{_}1112{_}Would you really like a headquarters post?"
10076-8{_}1113{_}Lister moved abruptly and his mouth got firm.
10076-8{_}1114{_}Perhaps Ruth exaggerated her father's importance, but it was possible Duveen could get him promotion.
10076-8{_}1115{_}All the same, Lister saw what his taking the job implied; he must give up his independence and be Duveen's man.
10076-8{_}1116{_}Moreover, if the girl meant to help, she had some grounds for doing so.
10076-8{_}1117{_}He thrilled and was tempted, but he thought hard.
10076-8{_}1118{_}It looked as if she liked him and was perhaps willing to embark upon a sentimental adventure, but he thought this was all.
10076-8{_}1119{_}She would not marry a poor man.
10076-8{_}1120{_}"No," he said, with a touch of awkwardness.
10076-8{_}1121{_}"I reckon I had better stick to the track.
10076-8{_}1122{_}To know where you properly belong is something, and if I took the other job, my chiefs would soon find me out."
10076-8{_}1123{_}"You're modest," Ruth remarked.
10076-8{_}1124{_}"One likes modest people, but don't you think you're obstinate?"
10076-8{_}1125{_}"When the trail you hit goes uphill, obstinacy's useful."
10076-8{_}1126{_}"If you won't take help, you may be long reaching the top, but we'll let it go.
10076-8{_}1127{_}The wind hasn't dropped much.
10076-8{_}1128{_}How can we get back?"
10076-8{_}1129{_}"We must wait," Lister replied with a twinkle.
10076-8{_}1130{_}"The trouble about an adventure is, when you start you're often forced to stay with it and put it over.
10076-8{_}1131{_}That sometimes costs more than you reckon."
10076-8{_}1132{_}Ruth's eyes sparkled, but she forced a smile.
10076-8{_}1133{_}"Logical people make me tired.
10076-8{_}1134{_}But why do you imagine I haven't the pluck to pay?"
10076-8{_}1135{_}"I don't," said Lister.
10076-8{_}1136{_}"I've no grounds to imagine anything like that.
10076-8{_}1137{_}My business was to take care of you and I ought to have seen the storm was coming.
10076-8{_}1138{_}Now I'm mad because I didn't watch out."
10076-8{_}1139{_}"Sometimes you're rather nice," Ruth remarked.
10076-8{_}1140{_}"You know I made you go on.
10076-8{_}1141{_}All the same, we must start as soon as possible."
10076-8{_}1142{_}Lister got up presently and launched the canoe.
10076-8{_}1143{_}The thunder had gone, but the breeze was strong and angry white waves rolled up the lake.
10076-8{_}1144{_}To drive the canoe to windward was heavy labor, and while she lurched slowly across the combers the sun got low.
10076-8{_}1145{_}Lister's wet hands blistered and his arms ached, but he swung the paddle stubbornly, and at length the houses and hotel stood out from the beach.
10076-8{_}1146{_}When they got near the landing Ruth looked ahead.
10076-8{_}1147{_}"The train's ready to pull out!"
10076-8{_}1148{_}she exclaimed.
10076-8{_}1149{_}"Can you make it?"
10076-8{_}1150{_}Lister tried.
10076-8{_}1151{_}His face got dark with effort and his hands bled, but in a few minutes he ran the canoe aground.
10076-8{_}1152{_}Ruth jumped out and they reached the station as the bell began to toll.
10076-8{_}1153{_}Duveen waved to them from the track by the front of the train and then jumped on board, and Lister pushed Ruth up the steps of the last car.
10076-8{_}1154{_}The car was second-class and crowded by returning holiday-makers, but the conductor, who did not know Lister and Miss Duveen, declared all the train was full and they must stay where they were.
10076-8{_}1155{_}When he went off and locked the vestibule Lister looked about.
10076-8{_}1156{_}All the seats and much of the central passage were occupied, for the most part by young men and women.
10076-8{_}1157{_}Some were frankly lovers and did not look disturbed by the banter of their friends.
10076-8{_}1158{_}Lister was embarrassed, for Ruth's sake, until he saw with some surprise that she studied the others with amused curiosity.
10076-8{_}1159{_}Looking down he met her twinkling glance and thought it something like a challenge.
10076-8{_}1160{_}His embarrassment got worse.
10076-8{_}1161{_}One could not talk because of the noise and to shout was ridiculous.
10076-8{_}1162{_}He must stand in a cramped pose and try not to fall against Ruth when the cars rocked.
10076-8{_}1163{_}He admitted that his proper background was the rude construction camp, and it was something of a relief when they rolled into Winnipeg.
10076-8{_}1164{_}Duveen's car was at the station, and Ruth stopped for a moment before she got on board.
10076-8{_}1165{_}"You start on Monday and we will be out of town to-morrow.
10076-8{_}1166{_}I wish you good luck."
10076-8{_}1167{_}Lister thanked her, and when she got into the car she gave him a curious smile.
10076-8{_}1168{_}"I think I liked you better in the woods," she said, and the car rolled off.
10076-8{_}1169{_}CHAPTER VII  LISTER'S DISSATISFACTION  Soon after his return from Winnipeg, Lister stood one evening by a length of track planned to cut out an awkward curve.
10076-8{_}1170{_}The new line ran into a muskeg that sucked down brush and logs and the loads of numerous gravel trains.
10076-8{_}1171{_}Angry foremen declared one could not fill up the bog, and Lister knew the heads of the construction office grumbled about the delay.
10076-8{_}1172{_}He was tired, for he had been strenuously occupied since morning, but could not persuade himself that the work had made much progress.
10076-8{_}1173{_}Small trees lay in tangled rows about the fresh gravel; farther back, the standing bush ran in a broken line against the fading light.
10076-8{_}1174{_}In front, thin mist drifted across the muskeg where slender trunks rose from the quaking mud.
10076-8{_}1175{_}Not far off a high, wooden trestle carried the rails across a ravine.
10076-8{_}1176{_}The bridge would presently be rebuilt with steel, but in the meantime the frame was open and the gaps between the ties were wide.
10076-8{_}1177{_}It was getting dark and noisy blast-lamps threw up pillars of white fire.
10076-8{_}1178{_}The line had sunk in the afternoon and it was necessary to lift the rails and fill up the subsidence before the next gravel train arrived.
10076-8{_}1179{_}Lister was angry and puzzled, for he had pushed the road-bed across to near the other side, but the rails had not sunk in the new belt but in ground over which the trains had run.
10076-8{_}1180{_}By and by a man joined him and remarked: "The boys have got the ties up, but I reckon they won't fix the track for three or four hours.
10076-8{_}1181{_}Looks as if the blamed muskeg was going to beat us."
10076-8{_}1182{_}"She can't beat us," Lister rejoined impatiently.
10076-8{_}1183{_}"The trouble is, hauling the stuff she swallows runs up construction costs, and that counts against us.
10076-8{_}1184{_}Did you leave Willis with the gang?"
10076-8{_}1185{_}The other laughed.
10076-8{_}1186{_}"I did not.
10076-8{_}1187{_}He was tired.
10076-8{_}1188{_}Wanted something at the office and allowed he'd stop and take a smoke."
10076-8{_}1189{_}"Hustle him out when you go along, Kemp.
10076-8{_}1190{_}I'd sooner our chiefs down East had kept that young man.
10076-8{_}1191{_}The job's not soft enough for him.
10076-8{_}1192{_}However, I s'pose he lighted the lamp across the bridge?"
10076-8{_}1193{_}"Willis has friends," Kemp remarked meaningly, and indicated a reflection behind the trees.
10076-8{_}1194{_}"The lamp's burning."
10076-8{_}1195{_}Lister glanced at the trembling light.
10076-8{_}1196{_}"I expect it's good enough for the engineer, but the flame's not steady.
10076-8{_}1197{_}Willis hasn't bothered to get the pressure right.
10076-8{_}1198{_}It's possible he didn't wait until she warmed the oil."
10076-8{_}1199{_}The powerful lamp had been carried across the bridge in order to warn the engineer of the gravel train, who on his last journey had run to the end of the line.
10076-8{_}1200{_}The light could be seen for some distance up the track.
10076-8{_}1201{_}"I got after Hardie about making good time.
10076-8{_}1202{_}We must dump his load in the soft spot before we stop," Lister resumed.
10076-8{_}1203{_}"He's coming now; climbing the height of land," said Kemp.
10076-8{_}1204{_}"He'll let her go all out when he makes the top."
10076-8{_}1205{_}A measured throb rolled across the woods, and as the noise got louder the beat of the exhaust marked the progress of the train.
10076-8{_}1206{_}The explosive snorts indicated that the locomotive labored up the last steep pitch, and Lister sat down by the rails.
10076-8{_}1207{_}He was tired and would not be needed until the gravel plough threw the rattling ballast off the cars.
10076-8{_}1208{_}After a few moments he looked up, for a man came out of the gloom.
10076-8{_}1209{_}"Hello, Willis!
10076-8{_}1210{_}I s'pose you've been taking a quiet smoke?"
10076-8{_}1211{_}"That's so," said the other.
10076-8{_}1212{_}"I've hustled round since sun-up and imagined the gang could get along for half an hour without my watching.
10076-8{_}1213{_}You want to leave something to your foremen."
10076-8{_}1214{_}Lister said nothing.
10076-8{_}1215{_}He did not choose his helpers, but tried to make the best use of those the bosses sent.
10076-8{_}1216{_}Willis had some useful qualities, but he was slack, and got sulky if one drove him hard.
10076-8{_}1217{_}The young man had come from the drawing-office of a famous bridge-building works.
10076-8{_}1218{_}In the meantime, the rumble of the gravel train grew to a pulsating roar.
10076-8{_}1219{_}The locomotive had crossed the divide and was running furiously down grade.
10076-8{_}1220{_}The roughly-ballasted track was uneven, but the engineer had been on board since daybreak and no doubt wanted to finish his job.
10076-8{_}1221{_}"She's in the rock cut now," Kemp remarked.
10076-8{_}1222{_}"Hardie ought to throttle down when he runs out and sees the light."
10076-8{_}1223{_}Lister listened.
10076-8{_}1224{_}The swelling note indicated that the train had left the cut, but it did not look as if the engineer was pulling up.
10076-8{_}1225{_}"She's coming along pretty fast," said Willis.
10076-8{_}1226{_}"If he doesn't snub her soon, she'll jump the steel and take the muskeg."
10076-8{_}1227{_}Next moment Lister was on his feet.
10076-8{_}1228{_}Hardie was driving too fast; Lister doubted if he could stop before the heavy train plunged through the broken track.
10076-8{_}1229{_}The unsteady white flicker behind the trees had sunk and changed to smoky red.
10076-8{_}1230{_}If looked as if the oil was not vaporizing properly and the lamp was going out.
10076-8{_}1231{_}When the engineer saw the light it would be too late.
10076-8{_}1232{_}"Get the boys off the track.
10076-8{_}1233{_}I'll try to fix the lamp," Lister shouted, and started for the bridge.
10076-8{_}1234{_}The errand was not his.
10076-8{_}1235{_}Willis had lighted the lamp: moreover, one might have sent a workman, but when a job was urgent Lister went himself.
10076-8{_}1236{_}The job was urgent and dangerous.
10076-8{_}1237{_}Unless he made good speed, he would meet the train on the bridge and the cylinders of the locomotive projected beyond the edge.
10076-8{_}1238{_}The track was rough and fresh gravel rolled under his feet.
10076-8{_}1239{_}Now and then he struck a cross-tie and nearly fell.
10076-8{_}1240{_}It had got dark and among the trees the gloom was deep; one could not see the ties.
10076-8{_}1241{_}Yet he must run, and his breath got labored and his heart thumped.
10076-8{_}1242{_}He did not know where the train was, only that it was near.
10076-8{_}1243{_}The woods throbbed with a savage din; the big cars, loaded with rattling gravel, clanged and roared as they plunged down grade.
10076-8{_}1244{_}Lister hardly thought he could stop the train.
10076-8{_}1245{_}It looked as if he would be caught on the trestle, but he meant to go on.
10076-8{_}1246{_}He did not argue about it; he was rather moved by instinctive stubbornness.
10076-8{_}1247{_}At moments of strain one does not argue and logic has no appeal.
10076-8{_}1248{_}Character counts for all, and Lister followed his bent.
10076-8{_}1249{_}His job was urgent and must be carried out.
10076-8{_}1250{_}When he reached the bridge he saw white threads of water between the timbers of the open frame.
10076-8{_}1251{_}The spacing of the ties was not regular, and if he stepped short, or too far, he would go through.
10076-8{_}1252{_}Then, if he did not strike a brace, he would fall upon the rocks in the stream.
10076-8{_}1253{_}All the same, he saw the blaze of the head-lamp pick out the trees across the ravine and sprang on to the bridge.
10076-8{_}1254{_}Somehow he hit the ties; perhaps by subconscious judgment, and perhaps by good luck.
10076-8{_}1255{_}Then he felt loose gravel under his feet and thrilled with a strange fierce satisfaction.
10076-8{_}1256{_}His breath was labored and his body wet by sweat, but the moving beam had not reached the lamp.
10076-8{_}1257{_}He was going to make it.
10076-8{_}1258{_}When the black front of a gravel car leaped out of the gloom he jumped off the track.
10076-8{_}1259{_}The locomotive pushed the cars, the train was long, and the lamp was but a few yards off.
10076-8{_}1260{_}It had not gone out, although the flame had sunk to a faint red jet that would not be seen in the dust.
10076-8{_}1261{_}His hands shook, but he gave the pump a few strokes and turned the valve wheel.
10076-8{_}1262{_}The red jet got white and leaped higher and Lister, pumping hard, looked up the track.
10076-8{_}1263{_}Big cars, rocking and banging, rushed past in a cloud of dust.
10076-8{_}1264{_}Bits of gravel struck him and rattled against the lamp.
10076-8{_}1265{_}The blurred, dark figures of men who sat upon the load cut against the fan-shaped beam, and in the background he saw a shower of leaping sparks.
10076-8{_}1266{_}But the other light was growing and Lister turned the wheel.
10076-8{_}1267{_}Burning oil splashed around him, a pillar of fire rushed up, and when a whistle screamed he let go the valve and turned from the blinding dust.
10076-8{_}1268{_}He was shaking, but the heavy snorting stopped.
10076-8{_}1269{_}The engineer had seen the light and cut off steam.
10076-8{_}1270{_}When Lister looked round the train was gone.
10076-8{_}1271{_}He had done what he had undertaken, and after waiting for a few moments he started back.
10076-8{_}1272{_}Now he could go cautiously, he stopped and tried to brace himself at the end of the bridge.
10076-8{_}1273{_}Although he had run across not long since, he shrank from the dark, forbidding gaps.
10076-8{_}1274{_}For all that, he must get back, and feeling carefully for the ties, he reached the other side and was for some time engaged at the muskeg where two cars had overrun the broken rails.
10076-8{_}1275{_}At length he went to the log shack he used for his office and sleeping-room, and soon after he lighted his pipe Kemp came in.
10076-8{_}1276{_}"You made it," Kemp remarked.
10076-8{_}1277{_}"When you stopped me at the bridge I saw you'd get there."
10076-8{_}1278{_}Lister laughed.
10076-8{_}1279{_}"Now you talk about it, I believe I did shout you to go back.
10076-8{_}1280{_}Anyhow, you were some way behind.
10076-8{_}1281{_}Did Willis come?"
10076-8{_}1282{_}"He did not.
10076-8{_}1283{_}Willis was badly rattled and started for the muskeg.
10076-8{_}1284{_}Thought he might get the track thrown across the hole, perhaps!
10076-8{_}1285{_}I'm rather sorry for the kid.
10076-8{_}1286{_}But what are you going to do about it?"
10076-8{_}1287{_}"Report we had two cars bogged and state the cost of labor.
10076-8{_}1288{_}That's all, I think."
10076-8{_}1289{_}Kemp nodded.
10076-8{_}1290{_}"Well, perhaps there's no use in talking about the lamp.
10076-8{_}1291{_}Our business is to make good, using the tools we've got.
10076-8{_}1292{_}All the same, if they want a man somewhere else, I guess I'd recommend Willis."
10076-8{_}1293{_}He smoked quietly for a time, and then resumed: "We don't get forward much.
10076-8{_}1294{_}In fact, if the new Western irrigation company would take me on, I think I'd quit."
10076-8{_}1295{_}Lister pondered.
10076-8{_}1296{_}Since his short stop at Winnipeg he had been conscious of a strange restlessness.
10076-8{_}1297{_}He wanted something the woods could not give, and had begun to think life had more to offer than he had known.
10076-8{_}1298{_}Besides, he was not making much progress.
10076-8{_}1299{_}"Since the double track is to be pushed on across the plains, the department will need a bigger staff and there ought to be a chance for some of us," he said.
10076-8{_}1300{_}"Then there's the new work with the long bridges on the lake section that will carry higher pay.
10076-8{_}1301{_}We're next on turn and have some claim.
10076-8{_}1302{_}They ought to move us up."
10076-8{_}1303{_}"I doubt.
10076-8{_}1304{_}We didn't come from a famous office, and it's not always enough to know your job."
10076-8{_}1305{_}"Somebody will get a better post, and if I'm lucky I'll stay.
10076-8{_}1306{_}If not, I think I'll try the irrigation works."
10076-8{_}1307{_}"I feel like that," Kemp declared.
10076-8{_}1308{_}"But suppose the irrigation people turn our application down?"
10076-8{_}1309{_}"Then I'll lie off for a time.
10076-8{_}1310{_}Except when I went, to McGill with money I earned on a wheat barge, I haven't stopped work since I was a boy.
10076-8{_}1311{_}Now I'm getting tired and think I'll pull out and go across to look at the Old Country.
10076-8{_}1312{_}My father was an Englishman, and I have some money to burn."
10076-8{_}1313{_}"A good plan," Kemp agreed.
10076-8{_}1314{_}"After a change you come back fresh with a stronger punch.
10076-8{_}1315{_}Well, if we're not put on to the lake section, we'll try the irrigation scheme."
10076-8{_}1316{_}He got up and went off, but Lister sat on his bunk and smoked.
10076-8{_}1317{_}The bunk was packed with swamp-grass on which his coarse Hudson's Bay blankets were laid, and the shack was bare.
10076-8{_}1318{_}Ragged slickers and old overalls occupied the wall, long gum-boots a corner.
10076-8{_}1319{_}A big box carried an iron wash-basin, and a small table some drawing instruments.
10076-8{_}1320{_}Lister was not fastidious, and, as a rule, did not stop long enough at one spot to justify his making his shack comfortable.
10076-8{_}1321{_}Besides, he found it necessary to concentrate on his work, and had not much time to think about refinements.
10076-8{_}1322{_}All the same, he felt the shack was dreary and his life was bleak.
10076-8{_}1323{_}He had not felt this until he went to Winnipeg.
10076-8{_}1324{_}On the whole, he had liked the struggle against physical obstacles.
10076-8{_}1325{_}It was his proper job, but the struggle was stern and sometimes exhausting, and his reward was small.
10076-8{_}1326{_}Now he wanted something different, and gave himself to vague and brooding discontent.
10076-8{_}1327{_}Ruth Duveen had broken his former tranquillity.
10076-8{_}1328{_}In a sense, she had awakened him, and he imagined she had meant to do so.
10076-8{_}1329{_}All the same, to think she loved him was ridiculous; she was rather experimenting with fresh material.
10076-8{_}1330{_}Yet she was accountable for his discontent.
10076-8{_}1331{_}She had helped him to see that while he labored in the woods he had missed much.
10076-8{_}1332{_}He wanted the society of cultivated women and men with power and influence; to use control instead of carrying out orders; and to know something of refinement and beauty.
10076-8{_}1333{_}After all, his father was a cultivated Englishman, although Lister imagined he had inherited qualities that helped him most from his Canadian mother.
10076-8{_}1334{_}It was all he had inherited, except some debts he had laboriously paid.
10076-8{_}1335{_}He admitted that to realize his ambitions might be hard, but he meant to try.
10076-8{_}1336{_}Canada was for the young and stubborn.
10076-8{_}1337{_}If his chiefs did not promote him, he would make a plunge, and if his new plan did not work, he would go over and see the Old Country.
10076-8{_}1338{_}Then he would come back, braced and refreshed, and try his luck again.
10076-8{_}1339{_}Putting down his pipe, he got into bed.
10076-8{_}1340{_}He was tired and in the morning the gravel cars must be pulled out of the muskeg.
10076-8{_}1341{_}The job was awkward, and while he thought about it he went to sleep.
10076-8{_}1342{_}CHAPTER VIII  THE TEST  A boisterous wind swept the high plain and round, white-edged clouds rolled across the sky.
10076-8{_}1343{_}The grass that ran back from the horizon was parched, and in the distance a white streak of blowing dust marked a dried alkali lake.
10076-8{_}1344{_}Dust of dark color drove along the row of wooden stores and houses that fronted the railroad track, across which three grain elevators rose like castles.
10076-8{_}1345{_}The telegraph posts along the track melted into the level waste, and behind the spot where they vanished the tops of a larger group of elevators cut the edge of the plain.
10076-8{_}1346{_}The street was not paved, and the soil was deeply ploughed by wheels.
10076-8{_}1347{_}The soil was the black gumbo in which the wheat plant thrives, but the town occupied the fringe of a dry belt and farming had not made much progress.
10076-8{_}1348{_}Now, however, a company was going to irrigate the land with water from a river fed by the Rockies' snow.
10076-8{_}1349{_}The town was square, and although it looked much smaller than real-estate agents' maps indicated, it was ornamented by four wooden churches, a Y.M.C.A.
10076-8{_}1350{_}like a temple, and an ambitious public hall.
10076-8{_}1351{_}The Tecumseh Hotel occupied a corner lot at the end of the street and was not remarkably commodious or clean, but its charges were less than the Occidental's by the station, and Lister and Kemp were not fastidious.
10076-8{_}1352{_}Some time had gone since they pulled the gravel cars out of the swamp and they had not been sent to the lake section.
10076-8{_}1353{_}In consequence, they had applied to the irrigation company for a post, and having been called to meet the engineers and directors, imagined they were on the short list.
10076-8{_}1354{_}Lister lounged against the rails on the Tecumseh veranda.
10076-8{_}1355{_}The boards were cracked and dirty; burned matches and cigar ends were scattered about, and a skeleton, gauze covered door that shut with a powerful spring kept some of the flies and mosquitoes out of the hotel.
10076-8{_}1356{_}"We'll know to-morrow," he remarked presently.
10076-8{_}1357{_}Kemp nodded.
10076-8{_}1358{_}"I can't figure on our chances.
10076-8{_}1359{_}Feel anxious about it?"
10076-8{_}1360{_}"Not much.
10076-8{_}1361{_}In fact, I mean to use the thing to test my luck.
10076-8{_}1362{_}If we're engaged, I'll stay in Canada; if they turn us down, I'll start for the Old Country."
10076-8{_}1363{_}"You have no particular plans, I reckon."
10076-8{_}1364{_}"No," said Lister, smiling.
10076-8{_}1365{_}"I'm going to look about.
10076-8{_}1366{_}I know our new Western towns, but I want to see old cities, churches, and cathedrals; the great jobs men made before they used concrete and steel.
10076-8{_}1367{_}Then I'd like to study art and music and see the people my father talked about.
10076-8{_}1368{_}Ours is a good country, but when it's all you know it gets monotonous."
10076-8{_}1369{_}He indicated the row of wooden houses and lonely plain.

10076-8{_}1372{_}"Looks as if the company's short list was pretty long.

10076-8{_}1375{_}he exclaimed.

10076-8{_}1377{_}"I came in on the last train.
10076-8{_}1378{_}Got a notice to meet the Irrigation Board."

10076-8{_}1382{_}"I'll sell you my chance for ten dollars," Kemp rejoined.

10076-8{_}1396{_}In the real West, the pictures were ridiculous, because romantic shootings-up did not happen.

10076-8{_}1479{_}It was part of the price he must pay for freedom.

10076-8{_}1497{_}"I need three or four drinks, but mean to go without," said Lister grimly.
10076-8{_}1498{_}"I begin to understand how some men get the tanking habit."
10076-8{_}1499{_}He started off across the plain, and coming back too late for lunch, found Kemp on the veranda.
10076-8{_}1500{_}Kemp looked as if he were trying to be philosophical, but found it hard.
10076-8{_}1501{_}"The secretary arrived not long since," he said.
10076-8{_}1502{_}"A polite man!

10076-8{_}1505{_}said Lister.

10076-8{_}1507{_}Kemp nodded.
10076-8{_}1508{_}"Willis has got the best job; they've hired up two or three others, but we're left out."
10076-8{_}1509{_}"Willis!"
10076-8{_}1510{_}exclaimed Lister, and joined in Kemp's laugh.

10076-8{_}1512{_}"In this country we're a curious lot.
10076-8{_}1513{_}We let grafters and wire-pullers run us, and, when we start a big job, get away with much of the capital we want for machines; but somehow we make good.
10076-8{_}1514{_}We shoulder a load we needn't carry and hit the pace up hot.
10076-8{_}1515{_}If we got clean control, I reckon we'd never stop.
10076-8{_}1516{_}However, there's not much use in philosophizing when you've lost your job, and the East-bound train goes out in a few minutes.
10076-8{_}1517{_}You'd better pack your grip."
10076-8{_}1518{_}CHAPTER IX  BARBARA PLAYS A PART  Lister returned to the railroad camp and stayed until the company sent a man to fill his post.
10076-8{_}1519{_}In the meantime, he wrote to some of his father's relations, whom he had not seen, and their reply was kind.
10076-8{_}1520{_}They stated that while he was in England he must make their house his home.
10076-8{_}1521{_}When his successor arrived he started for Montreal, and one afternoon sat under a tree in the square by the cathedral.
10076-8{_}1522{_}The afternoon was calm.
10076-8{_}1523{_}A thunderstorm that wet the streets had gone, and an enervating damp heat brooded over the city.
10076-8{_}1524{_}After the fresh winds that sweep the woods and plains, Lister felt the languid air made him slack and dull.
10076-8{_}1525{_}His steamer did not sail until daybreak, and since he had gone up the mountain and seen the cathedral and Notre Dame, he did not know what to do.
10076-8{_}1526{_}The bench he occupied was in the shade, and he smoked and looked about.
10076-8{_}1527{_}Cabs rolled up the street to the big hotel across the square, and behind the trees the huge block of the C.P.R.
10076-8{_}1528{_}station cut the sky.
10076-8{_}1529{_}One heard whistles, the rumble of heavy wheels, and the tolling of locomotive bells.
10076-8{_}1530{_}Pigeons flew down from the cathedral dome and searched the damp gravel.
10076-8{_}1531{_}A group of foreign emigrants picnicked in the shade.
10076-8{_}1532{_}Their clothes were old and greasy; they carried big shapeless bundles and looked tired and worn.
10076-8{_}1533{_}Lister could not guess their nationality, but imagined they had known poverty and oppression in Eastern Europe.
10076-8{_}1534{_}It was obvious they had recently disembarked from a crowded steerage and waited for an emigrant train.
10076-8{_}1535{_}They were going West, to the land of promise, and Lister wished them luck.
10076-8{_}1536{_}He and they were birds of passage and, with all old landmarks left behind, rested for a few hours on their journey.
10076-8{_}1537{_}He studied the group.
10076-8{_}1538{_}The men looked dull and beaten; the women had no beauty and had grown coarse with toil.
10076-8{_}1539{_}Their faces were pinched and their shoulders bent.
10076-8{_}1540{_}Only the children, in spite of rags and dirt, struck a hopeful note.
10076-8{_}1541{_}Yet the forlorn strangers had pluck; they had made a great adventure and might get their reward.
10076-8{_}1542{_}Lister had seen others in the West, who had made good, breaking soil they owned and walking with the confident step of self-respecting men.
10076-8{_}1543{_}On the plains, stubborn labor was rewarded, but one needed pluck to leave all one knew and break custom's familiar but heavy yoke.
10076-8{_}1544{_}By and by Lister remembered he wanted to take his relations a few typically Canadian presents.
10076-8{_}1545{_}He had seen nothing that satisfied him at Winnipeg, and had better look about the shops at Montreal.
10076-8{_}1546{_}Anyhow, it would amuse him for an hour or two.
10076-8{_}1547{_}He got up, went along the path for a few yards, and then stopped.
10076-8{_}1548{_}Across the clanging of the locomotive bells and the roll of trolley cars at the bottom of the hill he heard sweet voices.
10076-8{_}1549{_}The music was faint and somehow ethereal, as if it fell from a height.
10076-8{_}1550{_}One lost it now and then.
10076-8{_}1551{_}It came from the cathedral and Lister stopped and listened.
10076-8{_}1552{_}He did not know what office was being sung, but the jaded emigrants knew, for a child got up and stood with bent head, holding a greasy cap, and a ragged woman's face got gentle as she signed herself with the cross.
10076-8{_}1553{_}It looked as if the birds of passage had found a landmark in a foreign land.
10076-8{_}1554{_}Lister was moved, and gave the child a coin before he went off.
10076-8{_}1555{_}He strolled east, past Notre Dame, towards the post office, about which the stately banks and imposing office blocks stand.
10076-8{_}1556{_}This quarter of the city drew him, for one saw how constructive talent and imagination could be used, and he wondered whether England had new buildings like these.
10076-8{_}1557{_}Sometimes one felt the Western towns were raw and vulgar, but one saw the bold Canadian genius at its best in Montreal.
10076-8{_}1558{_}After a time he stopped in front of a shop in a short side street.
10076-8{_}1559{_}Indian embroidery work and enameled silver occupied the window, and although Lister was not an artist he had an eye for line and knew the things were good.
10076-8{_}1560{_}The soft, stained deerskin was cleverly embroidered; he liked the warm colors of the enamel, and going in was shown a tray of spoons.
10076-8{_}1561{_}The shop, shut in by high buildings, was dark and smelt of aromatic wood and leather, but a beam from a window pierced the gloom and sparkled on the silver.
10076-8{_}1562{_}This was emblazoned with the arms of the Provinces; the Ship, the Wheatsheaves, and the red Maple Leaf.
10076-8{_}1563{_}Lister picked up the articles, and while he did so was vaguely conscious that a girl at the opposite counter studied him.
10076-8{_}1564{_}He, however, did not look up until he had selected a few of the spoons, and then he started.
10076-8{_}1565{_}The light that touched the girl's face did not illuminate it all.
10076-8{_}1566{_}Her profile was sharp as an old daguerreotype: he saw the flowing line from brow to chin, drawn with something of austere classic beauty, the arched lips and the faint indication of a gently-rounded cheek.
10076-8{_}1567{_}The rest was in shadow, and the contrast of light and gloom was like a Rembrandt picture.
10076-8{_}1568{_}Then the enameled spoons rattled as Lister put down the tray.
10076-8{_}1569{_}He knew the picture.
10076-8{_}1570{_}When he last saw the girl, her face was lighted like that by the blaze of a locomotive head-lamp.
10076-8{_}1571{_}"I'll take these things," he said, and crossed the floor.
10076-8{_}1572{_}The girl moved back, but he indicated a bundle of deerskin articles he thought her business was to sell.
10076-8{_}1573{_}Her color was high; he noted the vivid white and pink against the dull background of stained leather.
10076-8{_}1574{_}"What does one do with those bags?"
10076-8{_}1575{_}he asked.
10076-8{_}1576{_}"They're useful for keeping gloves and handkerchiefs," she replied.
10076-8{_}1577{_}"The pattern is worked in sinews, but we have some with a neat colored embroidery."
10076-8{_}1578{_}She paused and signed to a saleswoman farther on.
10076-8{_}1579{_}"Will you bring this gentleman the Revillon goods?"
10076-8{_}1580{_}Lister's object for stopping her was not very plain, but he did not mean to let her go.
10076-8{_}1581{_}"Please don't bother.
10076-8{_}1582{_}I expect to find something in this bundle," he said to the approaching saleswoman.
10076-8{_}1583{_}Then he turned to the girl in front.

10076-8{_}1585{_}She gave him the bag, and although her glance was steady he knew she was embarrassed.

10076-8{_}1717{_}When her bows went down the shining swell broke with a dull roar and rainbows flickered in the spray about her forecastle; then, while the long deck got level, one heard the beat of engines and the grinding of screws.

10076-8{_}1719{_}Ahead an ice-floe glittered in the sun.
10076-8{_}1720{_}The liner had left Belle Isle Strait and was steaming towards Greenland on the northern Atlantic course.

10076-8{_}1868{_}You imagine he's something of a highbrow Englishman, rather formal and polite, but he has an eye like a fish-hawk's and his orders go.
10076-8{_}1869{_}Hair and mustache white; you don't know if his clothes are old or new, but you feel they're exactly what he ought to wear.
10076-8{_}1870{_}That's Cartwright, so to speak, on top; but when you meet him you want to remember you're not up against a Canadian.
10076-8{_}1871{_}We're a straight type.
10076-8{_}1872{_}When we're tough, we're very tough all the time; when we're cultivated, you can see the polish shine.
10076-8{_}1873{_}In the Old Country it's harder to fix where folks belong."
10076-8{_}1874{_}"You imply that you have got to know Cartwright before you fix him?"
10076-8{_}1875{_}Vernon laughed.
10076-8{_}1876{_}"I haven't quite fixed him yet.
10076-8{_}1877{_}At one time he's a sober gentleman of the stiff old school; at another he's as rough as the roughest hobo I've met in the West.
10076-8{_}1878{_}I reckon he'd beat a business crook at the other's smartest trick, but if you're out for a straight deal, you'll find Cartwright straight."
10076-8{_}1879{_}He went off to change some money and Lister went to his cabin and began to pack his trunk.
10076-8{_}1880{_}When he came up they had passed the Chicken Rock and a long bright beam touched the sea astern.
10076-8{_}1881{_}In the East, water and sky faded to dusky blue, but presently a faint light began to blink as if it beckoned.
10076-8{_}1882{_}The light got brighter and gradually drew abeam.
10076-8{_}1883{_}The foaming wake glimmered lividly in the dark, the beat of screws seemed quicker, and Lister thought the ship was carried forward by a stream of tide.
10076-8{_}1884{_}Other lights began to blink.
10076-8{_}1885{_}They stole out of the dark, got bright, and vanished, and Lister, leaning on the rails, felt they called him on.
10076-8{_}1886{_}One knew them by their colors and measured flashes.
10076-8{_}1887{_}They were beacons, burning on a well-ordered plan to guide the navigator, but he did not know the plan.
10076-8{_}1888{_}In a sense, this was important, and he began to muse.
10076-8{_}1889{_}Now he would soon reach the Old Country, he felt he had made a momentous plunge.
10076-8{_}1890{_}Adventure called, he knew Canada and wanted something fresh, but he wondered whether this was all.
10076-8{_}1891{_}Perhaps the plunge had, so to speak, not been a thoughtless caprice.
10076-8{_}1892{_}In a sense, things had led up to it and made it logical.
10076-8{_}1893{_}For example, it might not have been for nothing he met the girl on the train and got hurt.
10076-8{_}1894{_}His hurt had kept him at Winnipeg and stopping there had roused his discontent.
10076-8{_}1895{_}Then he had met Vernon, who wanted him to know the English ship-owner.
10076-8{_}1896{_}It was possible these things were like the flashes that leaped out of the dark.
10076-8{_}1897{_}He would know where they pointed when the journey was over.
10076-8{_}1898{_}Then Lister smiled and knocked out his pipe.
10076-8{_}1899{_}When he went on deck again some time afterwards the ship was steering for a gap between two rows of twinkling lights.
10076-8{_}1900{_}They ran on, closing on each other, like electric lamps in a long street, and in front the sky shone with a dull red glow.
10076-8{_}1901{_}It was the glimmer of a great port, they were entering the Mersey, and he went off to get up his luggage.
10076-8{_}1902{_}PART II--THE RECKONING    CHAPTER I  VERNON'S PLOT  Lister occupied the end of a slate-flag bench on the lawn at Carrock, Mrs. Cartwright's house in Rannerdale.
10076-8{_}1903{_}Rannerdale slopes to a lake in the North Country, and the old house stands among trees and rocks in a sheltered hollow.
10076-8{_}1904{_}The sun shone on its lichened front, where a creeper was going red; in the background birches with silver stems and leaves like showers of gold gleamed against somber firs.
10076-8{_}1905{_}Across the lawn and winding road, the tranquil lake reflected bordering woods; and then long mountain slopes that faded from yellow and green to purple closed the view.
10076-8{_}1906{_}While Lister waited for the tea Mrs. Cartwright had given him to cool he felt the charm of house and dale was strong.
10076-8{_}1907{_}Perhaps it owed something to the play of soft light and shade, for, as a rule, in Canada all was sharply cut.
10076-8{_}1908{_}The English landscape had a strange elusive beauty that gripped one hard, and melted as the fleecy clouds rolled by.
10076-8{_}1909{_}When the light came back color and line were as beautiful but not the same.
10076-8{_}1910{_}There was no grass in Canada like the sweep of smooth English turf, and Lister had not thought a house could give the sense of ancient calm one got at Carrock.
10076-8{_}1911{_}Since his boyhood he had not known a home; his resting place had been a shack at a noisy construction camp, a room at a crowded cheap hotel, and a berth beside a steamer's rattling engines.
10076-8{_}1912{_}Then the shining silver on the tea-table was something new; he marked its beauty of line, and the blue and gold and brown pattern on the delicate china he was almost afraid to touch.
10076-8{_}1913{_}In fact, all at Carrock was marked by a strange refinement and quiet charm.
10076-8{_}1914{_}He liked his hosts.
10076-8{_}1915{_}Mrs. Cartwright was large, rather fat, and placid, but he felt the house and all it stood for were hers by rightful inheritance.
10076-8{_}1916{_}Her son and daughter were not like that.
10076-8{_}1917{_}Lister thought they had cultivated their well-bred serenity and by doing so had cultivated out some virile qualities of human nature.
10076-8{_}1918{_}Grace Hyslop had beauty, but not much charm; Lister thought her cold, and imagined her prejudices were strong and conventional.
10076-8{_}1919{_}Mortimer's talk and manners were colorlessly correct.
10076-8{_}1920{_}Lister did not know yet if Hyslop was a prig or not.
10076-8{_}1921{_}Cartwright was frankly puzzling.
10076-8{_}1922{_}He looked like a sober country gentleman, and this was not the type Lister had thought to meet.
10076-8{_}1923{_}His clothes were fastidiously good, his voice had a level, restrained note, but his eye was like a hawk's, as Vernon had said.
10076-8{_}1924{_}Now and then one saw a twinkle of ironical amusement and some of his movements were quick and vigorous.
10076-8{_}1925{_}Lister thought Cartwright's blood was red.
10076-8{_}1926{_}Vernon, lounging at the opposite end of the bench, talked about a day Hyslop and he had spent upon the rocks, and rather struck a foreign note.
10076-8{_}1927{_}He had not Hyslop's graceful languidness; he looked alert and highly-strung.
10076-8{_}1928{_}His thin face was too grave for Carrock and his glance too quick.
10076-8{_}1929{_}Lister, listening to his remarks, was surprised to note that Hyslop was a bold mountaineer.
10076-8{_}1930{_}"Oh, well," he said, with a deprecatory smile, when Vernon stopped, "this small group of mountains is all the wild belt we have got, and you like to find a stranger keen about your favorite sport.
10076-8{_}1931{_}Then your keenness was flattering.
10076-8{_}1932{_}In your country, with its lonely woods and rivers running to the North, you have a field for strenuous sport and adventure."
10076-8{_}1933{_}"The woods pull," Vernon agreed.
10076-8{_}1934{_}"All the same, I'm a business man.
10076-8{_}1935{_}Betting at the Board of Trade is my proper job and I've got to be satisfied with a week at a fishing camp now and then.
10076-8{_}1936{_}Adventure is for the pioneers, lumber men and railroad builders like my friend."
10076-8{_}1937{_}Lister looked up.
10076-8{_}1938{_}He did not see why Vernon talked about him.
10076-8{_}1939{_}"My adventures don't count for much," he said.
10076-8{_}1940{_}"Sometimes a car went into a muskeg and we had to hustle to dig her out.
10076-8{_}1941{_}Sometimes the boys made trouble about their pay.
10076-8{_}1942{_}Railroad building is often dull."
10076-8{_}1943{_}"I don't know if we're all modest in Canada, but my partner is," Vernon observed.
10076-8{_}1944{_}"If you want a romantic tale, persuade him to tell you how he got the mark on his head."
10076-8{_}1945{_}"Oh shucks!"
10076-8{_}1946{_}said Lister.
10076-8{_}1947{_}"I had sooner you had cut that out."
10076-8{_}1948{_}He turned to the others apologetically.
10076-8{_}1949{_}"It was a dispute with a fellow on board a train who threw me down the steps.
10076-8{_}1950{_}I don't want to bore you with the tale."
10076-8{_}1951{_}"The man was the famous crook, Shillito," Vernon remarked.
10076-8{_}1952{_}Cartwright lifted his head and looked at Vernon hard.
10076-8{_}1953{_}Then he looked at Lister, who felt embarrassed and angry.
10076-8{_}1954{_}He saw Grace and Mrs. Cartwright were curious and thought Hyslop's glance got keen.
10076-8{_}1955{_}"If it will not bother Mr. Lister, we would like to hear his narrative," said Cartwright quietly, but Lister got a hint of command.
10076-8{_}1956{_}He narrated his adventure on the train, and although he tried to rob the story of its romance, was surprised when he stopped for a moment.
10076-8{_}1957{_}Vernon was carelessly lighting a cigarette, but Lister saw his carelessness was forced.
10076-8{_}1958{_}When he got a light he crossed the grass, as if he meant to throw the match over the hedge.
10076-8{_}1959{_}Lister thought Cartwright watched Harry with dry amusement.
10076-8{_}1960{_}Mrs. Cartwright's look was obviously disturbed, but she had not altogether lost her calm.
10076-8{_}1961{_}One felt her calm was part of her, but the Hyslops' was cultivated.
10076-8{_}1962{_}Lister imagined it cost them something to use control.
10076-8{_}1963{_}"Go on," said Cartwright, rather sharply.
10076-8{_}1964{_}Lister resumed, but presently Cartwright stopped him.
10076-8{_}1965{_}"You imagined the girl was afraid of Shillito!
10076-8{_}1966{_}What were your grounds?"
10076-8{_}1967{_}"She was disturbed and declared she must get off the train.
10076-8{_}1968{_}I think she meant to jump off, although we were going fast.
10076-8{_}1969{_}Then she asked me if the conductor could be bribed to stop."

10076-8{_}1976{_}It rather looked as if he weighed something carefully.
10076-8{_}1977{_}The lines on his face got deeper and his look was thoughtful.

10076-8{_}1980{_}How was she dressed?"
10076-8{_}1981{_}Lister was rather surprised to find he could not answer satisfactorily.
10076-8{_}1982{_}It was not the girl's physical qualities but her emotions he had marked.
10076-8{_}1983{_}He remembered the pluck with which she had struggled against the fear she obviously felt, her impulsive trust when he offered help, and her relief when she got into the locomotive cab.
10076-8{_}1984{_}Although he had studied her at Montreal, it was her effort to play a part that impressed him most.
10076-8{_}1985{_}"She was young, and I think attractive," he replied.
10076-8{_}1986{_}"She wore a knitted cap and a kind of jersey a girl might use for boating.
10076-8{_}1987{_}I thought she came from a summer camp."
10076-8{_}1988{_}Cartwright's face was inscrutable, but Lister saw the others' interest was keen.
10076-8{_}1989{_}Mrs. Cartwright's eyes were fixed on him and he got a hint of suspense.
10076-8{_}1990{_}Although Grace was very quiet, a touch of color had come to her skin, as if she felt humiliated.
10076-8{_}1991{_}Mortimer's pose was stiff and his control over done.
10076-8{_}1992{_}Then Cartwright turned to his step-daughter.
10076-8{_}1993{_}"Have you told Jones about the box of plants for Liverpool?"
10076-8{_}1994{_}Grace's look indicated that she did not want to go, but Cartwright's glance was insistent and she got up.
10076-8{_}1995{_}Lister looked about and saw Vernon had not come back.
10076-8{_}1996{_}He was studying the plants in a border across the lawn.

10076-8{_}1998{_}Lister fixed the date and added: "It was nearly ten o'clock.
10076-8{_}1999{_}The porter had just gone through the car and when he said my berth was ready I looked at my watch.
10076-8{_}2000{_}He went to the next Pullman, and I thought he was getting busy late."
10076-8{_}2001{_}Cartwright nodded and Mortimer glanced at him sharply, but next moment looked imperturbable.
10076-8{_}2002{_}Mrs. Cartwright's relief, however, was obvious.
10076-8{_}2003{_}Her face had become animated and her hands trembled.
10076-8{_}2004{_}"Thank you," said Cartwright.
10076-8{_}2005{_}"Go on."

10076-8{_}2009{_}Enough to buy a ticket East."

10076-8{_}2019{_}He had begun to see a light and wanted to finish and get away.
10076-8{_}2020{_}He did not, however, see that while he told his artless tale he had drawn his character.
10076-8{_}2021{_}When he stopped Cartwright said:  "Then you did not know her name?"

10076-8{_}2025{_}The gravel train was going East, and when the police boarded the cars we had run some distance West."
10076-8{_}2026{_}He stopped for a moment, because he saw he was very dull.

10076-8{_}2036{_}He got up.

10076-8{_}2038{_}Now I must get off, and I want to see Harry before I go."

10076-8{_}2043{_}So long as you stop here I hope you will feel our house is open to you."
10076-8{_}2044{_}Hyslop got up, but Cartwright stopped him with a sign.
10076-8{_}2045{_}He was quiet while they crossed the lawn, but when they reached the wood by the road he said, "I imagine you know we owe you much.
10076-8{_}2046{_}After a time, your efforts to use some tact were rather obvious.

10076-8{_}2048{_}"At the beginning, I did not know this," Lister declared.

10076-8{_}2053{_}"Why?"

10076-8{_}2064{_}Cartwright smiled.
10076-8{_}2065{_}"I'm going across as soon as possible to bring my step-daughter home."
10076-8{_}2066{_}CHAPTER II  BARBARA'S RETURN  When Lister had gone Cartwright returned to the tea-table and looked at Hyslop, who got up and went off.
10076-8{_}2067{_}Hyslop did not altogether want to go but he had cultivated discretion, and it was plain his step-father meant to get rid of him.
10076-8{_}2068{_}Then Cartwright gave his wife a sympathetic glance.
10076-8{_}2069{_}Mrs. Cartwright was calm, but when she put some cups together her hand shook.
10076-8{_}2070{_}"Leave the things alone," said Cartwright in a soothing voice.
10076-8{_}2071{_}"Vernon's plot was clever."
10076-8{_}2072{_}"Do you think Harry planned that Lister should tell us?"
10076-8{_}2073{_}"It looks like that," said Cartwright dryly.
10076-8{_}2074{_}"He was keen about bringing his friend over, but was cautious enough to wait until the fellow began to know us.
10076-8{_}2075{_}When he talked about Lister's adventures I wondered where he was leading.
10076-8{_}2076{_}The other was puzzled, and didn't see until near the end."
10076-8{_}2077{_}"But why didn't Harry, himself, tell us all he knew?"
10076-8{_}2078{_}"Vernon's a good sort and more fastidious than one thinks; he saw he'd be forced to venture on rather awkward ground, and there was some doubt.
10076-8{_}2079{_}He wanted us to weigh the story and judge if the clew he gave us ought to be followed.
10076-8{_}2080{_}This was not Vernon's job, although I think he was satisfied."
10076-8{_}2081{_}"But you are satisfied?"
10076-8{_}2082{_}"Yes," said Cartwright "Lister's portrait of Barbara was lifelike and his own was pretty good.
10076-8{_}2083{_}I think he drew himself and her better than he knew, and perhaps it's lucky we have to deal with fellows like these.
10076-8{_}2084{_}A good Canadian is a fine type.
10076-8{_}2085{_}However, we must bring Barbara back."
10076-8{_}2086{_}"Ah!"
10076-8{_}2087{_}said Mrs. Cartwright, "I want her back!
10076-8{_}2088{_}One must hide one's hurt, but to hide it is hard--" She pulled herself up and added: "Will you send a cablegram?"
10076-8{_}2089{_}"I think not.
10076-8{_}2090{_}The girl is proud and as wild as a hawk.
10076-8{_}2091{_}She thinks she has humiliated us, and if she's startled, she'll probably run away."
10076-8{_}2092{_}"You don't think she has humiliated us?"
10076-8{_}2093{_}Mrs. Cartwright said in a hesitating voice.
10076-8{_}2094{_}Cartwright smiled.
10076-8{_}2095{_}"It's plain that her escapade must not be talked about but we can trust these Canadians and I know Barbara.
10076-8{_}2096{_}In a sense, Lister's narrative wasn't necessary.
10076-8{_}2097{_}The girl is headstrong, but I was persuaded she would find the rascal out.
10076-8{_}2098{_}Looks as if she did so soon after they got on board the cars, and I imagine Shillito had an awkward few moments; Barbara's temper is not mild.
10076-8{_}2099{_}Then it's important that she was desperately anxious to escape from him.
10076-8{_}2100{_}There's no more to be said."
10076-8{_}2101{_}Mrs. Cartwright gave him a grateful look.
10076-8{_}2102{_}Her husband had never failed her and he had justified her trust again.
10076-8{_}2103{_}"If you don't send a cablegram, how shall we get Barbara back?"
10076-8{_}2104{_}"I'll go myself," said Cartwright "If she can't be persuaded, I'll bring her by force.
10076-8{_}2105{_}It's lucky I can charge the cost to the office.
10076-8{_}2106{_}The new wheat is coming down to Montreal, and the _Conference_ people have a plan to get it all, but I expect to beat them and engage some cargo for our boats before the St. Lawrence freezes.
10076-8{_}2107{_}However, since I'm going, I must get to work."
10076-8{_}2108{_}He started for the house and met his step-son at the porch.
10076-8{_}2109{_}Mortimer looked thoughtful, and held an unlighted cigarette.
10076-8{_}2110{_}Cartwright studied him with scornful amusement.
10076-8{_}2111{_}"Have you been speculating about the proper way of handling an awkward situation?"
10076-8{_}2112{_}"I have been talking to Grace," Hyslop replied in an even voice.
10076-8{_}2113{_}"I rather think Grace has been talking to you, but expect you agreed.
10076-8{_}2114{_}You have, no doubt, decided the best plan is to leave your headstrong sister alone?"
10076-8{_}2115{_}"We did agree about something like that," said Hyslop coolly, although when Cartwright fixed his eyes on his he turned his head.
10076-8{_}2116{_}"We thought if Barbara were given an allowance, she might, for example, stay with the Vernons.

10076-8{_}2118{_}When he was moved his urbanity vanished and his talk was very blunt.
10076-8{_}2119{_}"We'll let Grace's notion go.
10076-8{_}2120{_}My form is not my step-children's, but I try to moderate my remarks about women.
10076-8{_}2121{_}We'll admit Grace is a woman, although I sometimes doubt.

10076-8{_}2129{_}People might find out something and talk?
10076-8{_}2130{_}If anybody talks while I'm about, I'll ram the implication down his throat!

10076-8{_}2135{_}Hyslop went.

10076-8{_}2281{_}CHAPTER III  LISTER CLEARS THE GROUND  The sun was on the rocks and the lichen shone in rings of soft and varied color.
10076-8{_}2282{_}Blue shadows filled the dale, which, from the side of the Buttress, looked profoundly deep.
10076-8{_}2283{_}A row of young men and women followed a ledge that crossed the face of the steep crag; Mortimer Hyslop leading, a girl and Vernon a few yards behind, Lister and Barbara farther off.
10076-8{_}2284{_}Hyslop knew the rocks and was a good leader.
10076-8{_}2285{_}He was cool and cautious and did not undertake a climb until he was satisfied about his companions' powers.
10076-8{_}2286{_}The slanting edge looked dangerous, but was not, although one must be steady and there was an awkward corner.
10076-8{_}2287{_}At the turning, the ledge got narrow, and one must seize a knob and then step lightly on a stone embedded in mossy soil.
10076-8{_}2288{_}When they reached the spot Hyslop stopped and told Vernon what to do; the girl immediately behind him was a clever mountaineer.
10076-8{_}2289{_}They went round and Lister watched from a few yards off.
10076-8{_}2290{_}For a moment or two each in turn, supported by one foot with body braced against the rock, grasped the knob and vanished round the corner.
10076-8{_}2291{_}It was plain one must get a firm hold, but Lister thought this was all.
10076-8{_}2292{_}He was used to the tall skeleton trestles that carried the rails across Canadian ravines.
10076-8{_}2293{_}After the others disappeared Lister seized the knob.
10076-8{_}2294{_}He thought the stone he stood on moved and he cautiously took a heavier strain on his arm.
10076-8{_}2295{_}He could get across, but he obeyed an impulse and gave the stone a push.
10076-8{_}2296{_}It rolled out and, when he swung himself back to the ledge, plunged down and smashed upon the rocks below.
10076-8{_}2297{_}For a few moments the echoes rolled about the crags, and then Hyslop shouted: "Are you all right?
10076-8{_}2298{_}Can you get round?"
10076-8{_}2299{_}Lister said he thought not, and Hyslop replied that it did not matter.
10076-8{_}2300{_}Barbara would take him up a grassy ridge and the others would meet them at the top.
10076-8{_}2301{_}A rattle of nailed boots indicated that he was going off and Lister turned and glanced at Barbara.
10076-8{_}2302{_}She had sat down on an inclined slab and her figure and face, in profile, cut against the sky.
10076-8{_}2303{_}A yard or two beneath her, the sloping rock vanished at the top of a steep pitch and one saw nothing but the crags across the narrow dale.
10076-8{_}2304{_}Yet Lister thought the girl was not disturbed.
10076-8{_}2305{_}"I expect I was clumsy,'' he apologized.
10076-8{_}2306{_}"Well," she said, "it looks like that!"
10076-8{_}2307{_}He gave her a quick glance and pondered.
10076-8{_}2308{_}Although he had gone to Carrock since she came home, she had been strangely cold and, so to speak, aloof.
10076-8{_}2309{_}He had imagined their meeting might embarrass her, but she was not embarrassed.
10076-8{_}2310{_}In fact, she had met him as if he were a friend, but he had not seen her afterwards unless somebody was about.
10076-8{_}2311{_}Now he meant to force her to be frank.
10076-8{_}2312{_}"I was clumsy," he resumed.
10076-8{_}2313{_}"All the same, when I felt the stone begin to move I might have pulled myself across by my hands.
10076-8{_}2314{_}I expect the block would have been firm enough to carry you."
10076-8{_}2315{_}"Yes, I know," said Barbara.
10076-8{_}2316{_}"You didn't want me to get across!"
10076-8{_}2317{_}Lister studied her.
10076-8{_}2318{_}He doubted if it was altogether exertion that had brought the blood to her skin and given her eyes the keen sparkle.
10076-8{_}2319{_}Clinging to the rock, with the shadowy gulf below, she looked strangely alert and virile.
10076-8{_}2320{_}Her figure cut against the sky; he noted its slenderness and finely-drawn lines.
10076-8{_}2321{_}She was not angry, although he had admitted he pushed down the stone, but he felt as if something divided them and doubted if he could remove the obstacle.
10076-8{_}2322{_}"I wanted to talk and had found I could not get near you unless the others were about," he said.
10076-8{_}2323{_}"It looked as if I had unconsciously given you some grounds for standing me off.
10076-8{_}2324{_}Well, I suppose I did put your relations on your track."
10076-8{_}2325{_}"It wasn't that," said Barbara.
10076-8{_}2326{_}"I imagine Harry Vernon helped you there.
10076-8{_}2327{_}You were forced to tell your story."
10076-8{_}2328{_}"I was forced.
10076-8{_}2329{_}All the same, I think Harry's plan was good."
10076-8{_}2330{_}"He went away a few days before I arrived!"
10076-8{_}2331{_}Barbara remarked.
10076-8{_}2332{_}Lister thought he saw where she led and knitted his brows.
10076-8{_}2333{_}He was on awkward ground and might say too much, but to say nothing might be worse.

10076-8{_}2336{_}Although her color was vivid, Barbara gave him a searching glance.

10076-8{_}2338{_}Harry was at the camp in the woods."

10076-8{_}2372{_}"Sometimes one must trust one's luck, and venture.

10076-8{_}2401{_}"The hold is pretty good.
10076-8{_}2402{_}Do you think you can get up?"
10076-8{_}2403{_}Lister doubted.
10076-8{_}2404{_}He was athletic and steady, but the climb looked awkward for a beginner.
10076-8{_}2405{_}"If you are going, I'll try."
10076-8{_}2406{_}"You imagine you can go where I can go?"
10076-8{_}2407{_}"Something like that," Lister admitted.
10076-8{_}2408{_}"If I'm beaten, you're accountable and will have to help."
10076-8{_}2409{_}He was satisfied by Barbara's frank laugh.
10076-8{_}2410{_}Her mood was changeable.
10076-8{_}2411{_}Not long since he had, with awkward sympathy, thought her a proud humiliated woman; now she was marked by the humor of a careless girl.
10076-8{_}2412{_}He could, however, play up to her later mood, and when they set off he began to joke.
10076-8{_}2413{_}The rock slanted, and cracks and breaks gave a firm hold, but there was not a crack wherever one was needed and the pitch was steep.
10076-8{_}2414{_}Then in places the slabs were slippery with wet lichen and Lister's ordinary walking boots could get no grip.
10076-8{_}2415{_}His jokes stopped and the sweat began to dew his face.
10076-8{_}2416{_}His breath got hard and he felt his heart beat.
10076-8{_}2417{_}It was obvious that climbing needed study.
10076-8{_}2418{_}For all that, he went on and found a strange delight in watching Barbara.
10076-8{_}2419{_}Her clothes harmonized with the soft colors of lichen and stone; her movements were confident and light.
10076-8{_}2420{_}He got no sense of effort; her pose was seldom strained and the lines of her limbs and body flowed in easy curves.
10076-8{_}2421{_}He thought she rather flitted than labored up the rock.
10076-8{_}2422{_}Practice no doubt accounted for much, but something was due to temperament.
10076-8{_}2423{_}Barbara did not hesitate; she trusted her luck and went ahead.
10076-8{_}2424{_}At length she stopped, pressed against the stone in the hollow of a gully, while Lister crept obliquely across a long wet slab.
10076-8{_}2425{_}He looked up and saw her face, finely colored after effort, against a background of green and gold.
10076-8{_}2426{_}The berries on a small mountain-ash in a cranny harmonized with the carmine of her skin.
10076-8{_}2427{_}She looked down and smiled with careless amusement.
10076-8{_}2428{_}Then Lister's foot slipped and he could get no hold for his hands.
10076-8{_}2429{_}His smooth boots drew a greasy line across the wet slab as he slid down.
10076-8{_}2430{_}Perhaps the risk was not very daunting, but he knew he must not roll down far.
10076-8{_}2431{_}At the bottom of the slab he brought up with his foot braced against a knob, and he saw Barbara coming after him.
10076-8{_}2432{_}When she stopped her glance was apologetic.
10076-8{_}2433{_}"I forgot you hadn't proper boots.
10076-8{_}2434{_}Give me your hand and try again."
10076-8{_}2435{_}"No, thanks," said Lister.

10076-8{_}2438{_}she asked with a twinkle.

10076-8{_}2440{_}Then I expect I'm heavier than you think."

10076-8{_}2442{_}It would hurt to let a girl help," Barbara rejoined.
10076-8{_}2443{_}"After all, you're a conventionalist, and I rather thought you were not."
10076-8{_}2444{_}"Anyhow, I'm going up myself," Lister declared.
10076-8{_}2445{_}He got up, but his clothes gathered some slime from the rock and his skin was stained by soil and moss.
10076-8{_}2446{_}Barbara looked at him with a twinkle.
10076-8{_}2447{_}"Your obstinacy cost you something," she remarked.
10076-8{_}2448{_}"If you're tired, you had better stop and smoke."
10076-8{_}2449{_}Lister lighted a cigarette.
10076-8{_}2450{_}She had been rather keen about rejoining the others, but he thought she had forgotten.
10076-8{_}2451{_}Barbara's carelessness gave her charm.
10076-8{_}2452{_}Perhaps he ought to go on, but he meant to take the extra few minutes luck had given him.
10076-8{_}2453{_}"I'm really sorry I forgot about your boots and brought you up the rock," she said.
10076-8{_}2454{_}"I wonder why you did bring me up?"
10076-8{_}2455{_}"Oh, well, a number of the men I know have a comfortable feeling of superiority.
10076-8{_}2456{_}Of course, nice men don't make you feel this, but it's there.
10076-8{_}2457{_}One likes to give such pride a jolt."
10076-8{_}2458{_}"I think I see.
10076-8{_}2459{_}If it's some comfort, I'll own you can beat me going up awkward rocks.
10076-8{_}2460{_}But where does this take us?"
10076-8{_}2461{_}Barbara smiled.
10076-8{_}2462{_}"It takes us some distance.
10076-8{_}2463{_}When you admit a girl's your equal, friendship's easier.
10076-8{_}2464{_}You know, one reason Mortimer and I can't agree is, his feeling of superiority is horribly strong."

10076-8{_}2466{_}"No," said Barbara, in a regretful voice.
10076-8{_}2467{_}"He's really a good cragsman and knows exactly how far he can go.
10076-8{_}2468{_}When he starts an awkward climb he reckons up all the obstacles and is ready to get round them when they come.

10076-8{_}2470{_}People like Mortimer don't get stuck."
